# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Pod Eviction on Node Memory Pressure

## Your Task

Pods are evicted with reason 'memory pressure'. Find the Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that (1) define the memory pressure eviction thresholds and (2) implement the eviction manager's decision logic for memory-pressure-based pod eviction.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

41-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully identified and documented all the Go source files in the Kubernetes codebase that implement memory pressure pod eviction. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings:

### Memory Pressure Eviction Thresholds:
1. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_linux.go`** - Default threshold: 100Mi for Linux
2. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_windows.go`** - Default threshold: 500Mi for Windows
3. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/api/types.go`** - Signal definitions (SignalMemoryAvailable, SignalAllocatableMemoryAvailable)

### Eviction Manager Decision Logic:
1. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/eviction_manager.go`** - Main implementation:
   - `synchronize()` - Main control loop that monitors and triggers evictions
   - `IsUnderMemoryPressure()` - Checks current memory pressure state
   - `Admit()` - Admission handler that rejects pods during memory pressure

2. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers.go`** - Core eviction logic:
   - `thresholdsMet()` - Checks if memory thresholds are crossed
   - `rankMemoryPressure()` - Ranks pods for eviction priority
   - `makeSignalObservations()` - Collects current memory statistics

3. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers_others.go`** and **`helpers_windows.go`** - Platform-specific memory signal creation

### Eviction Flow:
The system continuously monitors memory availability, compares it against configured thresholds (default 100Mi on Linux), and when breached, evicts pods in priority order: BestEffort pods first, then pods exceeding their memory requests, then by priority and usage.

The complete analysis has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

Here's how it works:\\n\\n**Threshold Definition:**\\nMemory pressure eviction thresholds are defined in platform-specific files:\\n- `pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_linux.go` and `defaults_others.go` define DefaultEvictionHard with a default memory.available threshold of 100Mi\\n- `pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_windows.go` defines DefaultEvictionHard with a default memory.available threshold of 500Mi\\n- `pkg/kubelet/eviction/api/types.go` defines the signal types: SignalMemoryAvailable (\\\"memory.available\\\") and SignalAllocatableMemoryAvailable (\\\"allocatableMemory.available\\\")\\n\\n**Eviction Manager Implementation:**\\n`pkg/kubelet/eviction/eviction_manager.go` contains the managerImpl struct, which is the main eviction manager. This ensures BestEffort pods and pods exceeding their requests are evicted first.\\n\\n**Platform-Specific Memory Signal Creation:**\\n- `pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers_others.go` (non-Windows): `makeMemoryAvailableSignalObservation()` creates memory signal observations from summary.Node.Memory.AvailableBytes and WorkingSetBytes\\n- `pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers_windows.go` (Windows): Similar platform-specific implementation with Windows-specific memory calculations\\n\\n**Signal-to-Condition Mapping:**\\nIn `pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers.go` (init function, lines 75-99), eviction signals are mapped to node conditions:\\n- SignalMemoryAvailable and SignalAllocatableMemoryAvailable both map to NodeMemoryPressure\\nThis allows the eviction manager to set the NodeMemoryPressure condition when memory thresholds are crossed.\\n\\n**Complete Eviction Flow:**\\n1. kubelet calls evictionManager.Start() which starts the control loop\\n2. Current memory stats are collected via makeSignalObservations()\\n4. thresholdsMet() checks if memory.available < configured threshold (default 100Mi on Linux)\\n5.
